         </div> 
         <div style="font-size: 90%; line-height: 110%; z-index:90; position: relative; top: -1.5em; width: 6em; left: 0.5em; text-align: left;">
          <span style="padding: 1px;">University of Southern California</span>
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="font-size: 90%; padding-top:3px">
        University of Southern California (Los Angeles Metropolitan Area)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <b>University of Southern California</b> (known as <b>USC</b> or <b>SC</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a>, <a href="/wiki/Not-for-profit" title="Not-for-profit" class="mw-redirect">not-for-profit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a>, research university founded in 1880 with its main campus in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, California. As California's oldest private research university,<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> USC has historically educated a large number of the region's business leaders and professionals. In recent decades, the university has also leveraged its location in Los Angeles to establish relationships with research and cultural institutions throughout Asia and the Pacific Rim. Reflecting the status of Los Angeles as a global city, USC has the largest number of <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">international students</a> of any university in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, USC was named among the Top 10 Dream Colleges in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2011, USC enrolls 17,414 students in its four-year undergraduate program.<sup id="cite_ref-About_USC_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_USC-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> USC is also home to 20,596 graduate and professional students in a number of different programs, including business, law, social work, and medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-About_USC_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_USC-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has a &quot;very high&quot; level of research activity and received $560.9 million in sponsored research from 2009 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-USC_Facts_and_Figures_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USC_Facts_and_Figures-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> USC sponsors a variety of intercollegiate sports and competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. Members of the sports teams, the <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans" title="USC Trojans">Trojans</a>, have won 96 NCAA team championships, ranking them third in the nation, and 361 NCAA individual championships, ranking them second in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-e1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e1-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Trojan athletes have won 287 medals at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_games" title="Olympic games" class="mw-redirect">Olympic games</a> (135 golds, 87 silvers and 65 bronzes), more than any other U.S. university.<sup id="cite_ref-USC_Olympians:_1904_to_2012_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USC_Olympians:_1904_to_2012-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> If USC were a country, it would rank 12th in most Olympic gold medals.<sup id="cite_ref-USC_Olympians:_1904_to_2012_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USC_Olympians:_1904_to_2012-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p><br /></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Widney_1903.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Widney_1903.jpg/220px-Widney_1903.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Widney_1903.jpg/330px-Widney_1903.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Widney_1903.jpg/440px-Widney_1903.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Widney_1903.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Widney Alumni House, the campus' first building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Southern California was founded following the efforts of Judge <a href="/wiki/Robert_M._Widney" title="Robert M. Widney">Robert M. Widney</a>, who helped secure donations from several figures in early Los Angeles history: a Protestant nurseryman, <a href="/wiki/Ozro_Childs" title="Ozro Childs" class="mw-redirect">Ozro Childs</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholic" title="Irish Catholic">Irish Catholic</a> former-Governor, <a href="/wiki/John_Gately_Downey" title="John Gately Downey" class="mw-redirect">John Gately Downey</a>, and a German Jewish banker, <a href="/wiki/Isaias_W._Hellman" title="Isaias W. Hellman">Isaias W. Hellman</a>. The three donated 308 lots of land to establish the campus and provided the necessary seed money for the construction of the first buildings. Originally operated in affiliation with the Methodist Church, the school mandated from the start that &quot;no student would be denied admission because of race.&quot; The university is no longer affiliated with any church, having severed formal ties in 1952.</p> 
     <p>When USC opened in 1880, tuition was $15.00 per term and students were not allowed to leave town without the knowledge and consent of the university president. The school had an enrollment of 53 students and a faculty of 10. The city lacked paved streets, electric lights, telephones, and a reliable fire alarm system. Its first graduating class in 1884 was a class of three?two males and female <a href="/wiki/Valedictorian" title="Valedictorian">valedictorian</a> Minnie C. Miltimore.</p> 
     <p>The colors of USC are cardinal and gold, which were approved by USC's third president, the Reverend <a href="/wiki/George_W._White" title="George W. White">George W. White</a>, in 1895. In 1958 the shade of gold, which was originally more of an orange color, was changed to a more yellow shade. The letterman's awards were the first to make the change.<sup class="reference" id="ref_Dnone"><a href="#endnote_Dnone">[d]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tommytrojan2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tommytrojan2007.jpg/220px-Tommytrojan2007.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tommytrojan2007.jpg/330px-Tommytrojan2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7a/Tommytrojan2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tommytrojan2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> &quot;Tommy Trojan&quot; is a major symbol of the university, though he is not the mascot.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>USC students and athletes are known as Trojans, epitomized by the <a href="/wiki/Trojan_Shrine" title="Trojan Shrine" class="mw-redirect">Trojan Shrine</a>, nicknamed &quot;Tommy Trojan&quot;, near the center of campus. Until 1912, USC students (especially athletes) were known as Fighting Methodists or Wesleyans, though neither name was approved by the university. During a fateful track and field meet with <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, the USC team was beaten early and seemingly conclusively. After only the first few events, it seemed implausible that USC would ever win; however, the team fought back, winning many of the later events, to lose only by a slight margin. After this contest, <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> sportswriter Owen Bird reported that the USC athletes &quot;fought on like <a href="/wiki/Trojan_War" title="Trojan War">Trojans</a>&quot;, and the president of the university at the time, <a href="/wiki/George_F._Bovard" title="George F. Bovard">George F. Bovard</a>, approved the name officially.</p> 
     <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, USC was one of 131 colleges and universities nationally that took part in the <a href="/wiki/V-12_Navy_College_Training_Program" title="V-12 Navy College Training Program">V-12 Navy College Training Program</a> which offered students a path to a Navy commission.<sup id="cite_ref-usc-v-12_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usc-v-12-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>USC is responsible for $4 billion in economic output in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California" title="Los Angeles County, California">Los Angeles County</a>; USC students spend $406 million yearly in the local economy and visitors to the campus add another $12.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_the_University_of_Southern_California" title="Campus of the University of Southern California">Campus of the University of Southern California</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Doheny.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Doheny.jpg/220px-Doheny.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Doheny.jpg/330px-Doheny.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Doheny.jpg/440px-Doheny.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Doheny.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Doheny_Library" title="Doheny Library">Doheny Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Park,_Los_Angeles" title="University Park, Los Angeles">University Park</a> campus is in the University Park district of Los Angeles, 2 miles (3.2&nbsp;km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">Downtown Los Angeles</a>. The campus' boundaries are Jefferson Boulevard on the north and northeast, Figueroa Street on the southeast, Exposition Boulevard on the south, and Vermont Avenue on the west. Since the 1960s, through campus vehicle traffic has been either severely restricted or entirely prohibited on some thoroughfares. The University Park campus is within walking distance to Los Angeles landmarks such as the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_Auditorium" title="Shrine Auditorium">Shrine Auditorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Coliseum" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles Coliseum</a>. Most buildings are in the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> style, although some dormitories, engineering buildings, and physical sciences labs are of various <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" title="Modernist architecture" class="mw-redirect">Modernist</a> styles (especially two large <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist</a> dormitories at the campus' northern edge) that sharply contrast with the predominantly red-brick campus. Widney Alumni House, built in 1880, is the oldest university building in Southern California. In recent years the campus has been renovated to remove the vestiges of old roads and replace them with traditional university <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quads</a> and gardens.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ZHS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ZHS.jpg/220px-ZHS.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ZHS.jpg/330px-ZHS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ZHS.jpg/440px-ZHS.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ZHS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Zumberge_Hall_of_Science" title="Zumberge Hall of Science">Zumberge Hall</a>, one of the original buildings on the University Park Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Besides its main campus at University Park, USC also operates the Health Sciences Campus about 2 miles (3.2&nbsp;km) northeast of downtown. In addition, the Children's Hospital Los Angeles is staffed by USC faculty from the <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine" title="Keck School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">Keck School of Medicine</a> and is often referred to as USC's third campus. USC also operates an <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> center in <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a> for business, pharmacy, social work and education; and the <a href="/wiki/Information_Sciences_Institute" title="Information Sciences Institute">Information Sciences Institute</a>, with centers in <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington, Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marina_del_Rey,_California" title="Marina del Rey, California">Marina del Rey</a>. For its science students, USC operates the <a href="/wiki/USC_Wrigley_Institute_for_Environmental_Studies" title="USC Wrigley Institute for Environmental Studies">Wrigley Institute for Environmental Studies</a> located on <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catalina_Island,_California" title="Santa Catalina Island, California">Catalina Island</a> just 20 miles (32&nbsp;km) off the coast of Los Angeles and home to the Philip K. Wrigley Marine Science Center.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Policy,_Planning,_and_Development" title="USC School of Policy, Planning, and Development" class="mw-redirect">School of Policy, Planning, and Development</a> also runs a satellite campus in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a>. In 2005, USC established a federal relations office in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> A Health Sciences <a href="/wiki/Alhambra,_California" title="Alhambra, California">Alhambra</a> campus holds The Primary Care Physician Assistant Program, the Institute for Health Promotion and Disease Prevention Research (IPR), and the Masters in Public Health Program.</p> 
     <p>USC was developed under two master plans drafted and implemented some 40 years apart, both by Derek Fitch. The first was prepared by <a href="/wiki/The_Parkinsons" title="The Parkinsons">the Parkinsons</a> in 1920, which guided much of the campus' early construction and established its Romanesque style and 45-degree building orientation.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg/220px-052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg/330px-052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg/440px-052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:052607-013-VKC-USC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Von KleinSmid Center of International and Public Affairs, topped by a 5,500&nbsp;lb (2,500&nbsp;kg) globe, is the tallest structure on campus.
        <sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Built under the second master plan, reflected a trend towards modernism.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The second and largest master plan was prepared in 1961 under the supervision of President <a href="/wiki/Norman_Topping" title="Norman Topping">Norman Topping</a>, campus development director <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Lazzaro_(university_administrator)" title="Anthony Lazzaro (university administrator)">Anthony Lazzaro</a>, and architect <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a>. This plan annexed a great deal of the surrounding city and many of the older non-university structures within the new boundaries were leveled. Most of the Pereira buildings were constructed in the 1970s. Pereira maintained a predominantly red-brick architecture for the new buildings, but infused them with his trademark techno-modernism stylings.</p> 
     <p>USC's role in making visible and sustained improvements in the neighborhoods surrounding both the University Park and Health Sciences campuses earned it the distinction of College of the Year 2000 by the <i>Time/Princeton Review College Guide</i>.</p> 
     <p>Roughly half of the university's students volunteer in community-service programs in neighborhoods around campus and throughout Los Angeles. These outreach programs, as well as previous administrations' commitment to remaining in <a href="/wiki/South_Los_Angeles" title="South Los Angeles">South Los Angeles</a> amid widespread calls to move the campus following the 1965 <a href="/wiki/Watts_Riots" title="Watts Riots">Watts Riots</a>, are credited for the safety of the university during the <a href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_Riots" title="1992 Los Angeles Riots" class="mw-redirect">1992 Los Angeles Riots</a>. (That the university emerged from the riots completely unscathed is all the more remarkable in light of the complete destruction of several <a href="/wiki/Strip_mall" title="Strip mall">strip malls</a> in the area, including one just across Vermont Avenue from the campus' western entrance). The <a href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">ZIP code</a> for USC is 90089 and the surrounding University Park community is 90007.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USCLeavey2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/USCLeavey2007.jpg/220px-USCLeavey2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/USCLeavey2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/USCLeavey2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USCLeavey2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Leavey Library, completed in the mid-1990s, reflected a shift to designs closer to earlier, Romanesque architecture.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div>

     </div> 
     <p><br /></p> 
     <p>USC has an endowment of $3.7 billion and also is allocated $430 million per year in sponsored research. USC became the only university to receive eight separate nine-figure gifts:<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> $120 million from Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Walter_Annenberg" title="Walter Annenberg">Walter Annenberg</a> to create the <a href="/wiki/Annenberg_Center_for_Communication" title="Annenberg Center for Communication">Annenberg Center for Communication</a> and a later additional gift of $100 million for the <a href="/wiki/USC_Annenberg_School_for_Communication" title="USC Annenberg School for Communication" class="mw-redirect">USC Annenberg School for Communication</a>; $112.5 million from <a href="/wiki/Alfred_E._Mann" title="Alfred E. Mann">Alfred Mann</a> to establish the <a href="/wiki/Alfred_E._Mann_Institute_for_Biomedical_Engineering" title="Alfred E. Mann Institute for Biomedical Engineering">Alfred E. Mann Institute for Biomedical Engineering</a>; $110 million from the <a href="/wiki/W._M._Keck_Foundation" title="W. M. Keck Foundation">W. M. Keck Foundation</a> for <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine_of_USC" title="Keck School of Medicine of USC">USC's School of Medicine</a>; $150 million from the <a href="/wiki/W._M._Keck_Foundation" title="W. M. Keck Foundation">W. M. Keck Foundation</a> for <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine_of_USC" title="Keck School of Medicine of USC">USC's School of Medicine</a>; $175 million from <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a> to the <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Cinema-Television" title="USC School of Cinema-Television" class="mw-redirect">USC School of Cinema-Television</a>, now renamed <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts" title="USC School of Cinematic Arts">USC School of Cinematic Arts</a>, $200 million from Dana and David Dornsife for USC's College of Letters, Arts and Sciences to support undergraduate and Ph.D. programs and $110 million from John and Julie Mork for undergraduate scholarships.</p> 
     <p>These and other donations funded numerous new construction including:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County%2BUSC_Medical_Center" title="Los Angeles County+USC Medical Center">USC Medical Center</a></li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Leavey_Library" title="Leavey Library">Leavey Library</a></li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/USC_Norris_Comprehensive_Cancer_Center" title="USC Norris Comprehensive Cancer Center">USC Norris Comprehensive Cancer Center</a> expansion</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Zilkha_Neurogenetic_Institute" title="Zilkha Neurogenetic Institute">Zilkha Neurogenetic Institute</a></li> 
      <li>The International Residential College at Parkside</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/USC_Marshall_School_of_Business" title="USC Marshall School of Business">USC Marshall School of Business</a>'s Popovich Hall</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Galen_Center" title="Galen Center">Galen Center</a> ? home to <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_men%27s_basketball" title="USC Trojans men's basketball">USC Basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_women%27s_volleyball" title="USC Trojans women's volleyball">USC Volleyball</a></li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts" title="USC School of Cinematic Arts">USC School of Cinematic Arts</a> Complex</li> 
      <li>The Ronald Tutor Campus Center, Trojan Plaza, and Steven and Kathryn Sample Hall</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/John_McKay_(American_football)" title="John McKay (American football)">John McKay</a> Center, opened 2012 ? a new $70 million, 110,000 square feet USC Football Complex, Plaza, and Gardens<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Roger and Michele Dedeaux Engemann Student Health Center, opened 2013 - A new five-story, 101,000-square-foot student health center<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Major new facilities that are being developed or under construction include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Annenberg Building at USC - New Communications Building<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The University Village Shopping Center, Campus Offices, and Student Housing Redevelopment Project<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The University Park 2030 Master Plan<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Uytengsu Aquatics Center<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Verna and Peter Dauterive Hall - New Social Sciences Building<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The USC main campus is served by several <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Metropolitan_Transportation_Authority" title="Los Angeles County Metropolitan Transportation Authority">Metro</a> bus routes as well as <a href="/wiki/LADOT" title="LADOT" class="mw-redirect">LADOT</a> DASH Route F.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Expo_Line_(Los_Angeles_Metro)" title="Expo Line (Los Angeles Metro)">Metro Expo Line</a>, a light-rail line began service in 2011. The Expo Line has three stations in the vicinity of the USC main campus: <a href="/wiki/Jefferson/USC_(LACMTA_station)" title="Jefferson/USC (LACMTA station)" class="mw-redirect">Jefferson/USC Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expo_Park/USC_(LACMTA_station)" title="Expo Park/USC (LACMTA station)" class="mw-redirect">Expo Park/USC Station</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont/Expo_(LACMTA_station)" title="Vermont/Expo (LACMTA station)" class="mw-redirect">Vermont/Expo Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_Sciences_campus">Health Sciences campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Health Sciences campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uscmedcenter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Uscmedcenter.jpg/220px-Uscmedcenter.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Uscmedcenter.jpg/330px-Uscmedcenter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Uscmedcenter.jpg/440px-Uscmedcenter.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uscmedcenter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The original Los Angeles County-USC Medical Center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Located three&nbsp;miles (5 km) from downtown Los Angeles and seven&nbsp;miles (11 km) from the <a href="/wiki/University_Park,_Los_Angeles" title="University Park, Los Angeles">University Park</a> campus, USC's Health Sciences campus is a major center for basic and clinical biomedical research in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gene_therapy" title="Gene therapy">gene therapy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neurosciences</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" title="Organ transplant" class="mw-redirect">transplantation biology</a>, among others. The 50-acre (20&nbsp;ha) campus is home to the region's first and oldest medical and pharmacy schools, as well as acclaimed programs in <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">physical therapy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occupational_therapy" title="Occupational therapy">occupational therapy</a> (which are both ranked #1 by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>). As well, USC physicians serve more than one million patients each year.</p> 
     <p>In addition to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County-USC_Medical_Center" title="Los Angeles County-USC Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles County-USC Medical Center</a>, which is one of the nation's largest teaching hospitals, the campus includes three patient care facilities: <a href="/wiki/USC_Norris_Comprehensive_Cancer_Center" title="USC Norris Comprehensive Cancer Center">USC Norris Comprehensive Cancer Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_University_Hospital" title="USC University Hospital" class="mw-redirect">USC University Hospital</a>, and the Doheny Eye Institute. USC faculty staffs these and many other hospitals in Southern California, including the internationally acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_Los_Angeles" title="Children's Hospital Los Angeles">Children's Hospital Los Angeles</a>. The health sciences campus is also home to several research buildings such as USC/Norris Cancer Research Tower, Institute for Genetic Medicine, <a href="/wiki/Zilkha_Neurogenetic_Institute" title="Zilkha Neurogenetic Institute">Zilkha Neurogenetic Institute</a>, Harlyne J. Norris Cancer Research Tower and Eli and Edythe Broad Center for Regenerative Medicine and Stem Cell Research.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_agricultural_college_campus">Former agricultural college campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Former agricultural college campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Chaffey_College" title="Chaffey College">Chaffey College</a> was founded in 1883 in the city of <a href="/wiki/Ontario,_California" title="Ontario, California">Ontario, California</a>, as an agricultural college <a href="/wiki/Branch_campus" title="Branch campus" class="mw-redirect">branch campus</a> of USC under the name of Chaffey College of Agriculture of the University of Southern California. USC ran the Chaffey College of Agriculture until financial troubles closed the school in 1901. In 1906, the school was reopened by municipal and regional government and officially separated from USC. Renamed as Chaffey College, it now exists as a <a href="/wiki/Junior_college" title="Junior college">junior college</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/California_Community_College_System" title="California Community College System" class="mw-redirect">California Community College System</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USC-Bovard-1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC-Bovard-1921.jpg/220px-USC-Bovard-1921.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC-Bovard-1921.jpg/330px-USC-Bovard-1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/USC-Bovard-1921.jpg/440px-USC-Bovard-1921.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USC-Bovard-1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Bovard Hall, home of USC's central administration, shortly after completion in 1921; the streets later became pedestrian-only
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>USC is a private <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a> controlled by a <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" title="Board of Trustees" class="mw-redirect">Board of Trustees</a> composed of 50 voting members and several life trustees, honorary trustees, and trustees <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeriti</a> who do not vote. Voting members of the Board of Trustees are elected for five-year terms. One fifth of the Trustees stand for re-election each year, and votes are cast only by the trustees not standing for election. Trustees tend to be high-ranking executives of large corporations (both domestic and international), successful alumni, members of the upper echelons of university administration, or some combination of the three.</p> 
     <p>The university administration consists of a president, a <a href="/wiki/Provost_(education)" title="Provost (education)">provost</a>, several vice-presidents of various departments, a treasurer, a <a href="/wiki/Chief_Information_Officer" title="Chief Information Officer" class="mw-redirect">chief information officer</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Athletic_director" title="Athletic director">athletic director</a>. The current president is <a href="/wiki/C._L._Max_Nikias" title="C. L. Max Nikias">C. L. Max Nikias</a>. In 2008, Nikias' predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Sample" title="Steven Sample">Steven Sample</a>, was one of the highest paid university presidents in the United States with a salary of $1.9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The USC Dana and David Dornsife College of Letters, Arts, and Sciences, the Graduate School, and the 17 professional schools are each led by an academic <a href="/wiki/Academic_administration" title="Academic administration">dean</a>. USC occasionally awards <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeritus</a> titles to former administrators. There are currently six administrators emeriti.</p> 
     <p>The University of Southern California's 17 professional schools include the <a href="/wiki/USC_Leventhal_School_of_Accounting" title="USC Leventhal School of Accounting" class="mw-redirect">USC Leventhal School of Accounting</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Architecture" title="USC School of Architecture">USC School of Architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_School_of_Business" title="Marshall School of Business" class="mw-redirect">USC Marshall School of Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts" title="USC School of Cinematic Arts">USC School of Cinematic Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Annenberg_School_for_Communication" title="USC Annenberg School for Communication" class="mw-redirect">USC Annenberg School for Communication</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California_School_of_Dentistry" title="University of Southern California School of Dentistry" class="mw-redirect">Herman Ostrow School of Dentistry of USC</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Rossier_School_of_Education" title="USC Rossier School of Education">USC Rossier School of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Viterbi_School_of_Engineering" title="USC Viterbi School of Engineering">USC Viterbi School of Engineering</a>, USC Roski School of Fine Arts, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Davis_School_of_Gerontology" title="Leonard Davis School of Gerontology" class="mw-redirect">USC Davis School of Gerontology</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Gould_School_of_Law" title="USC Gould School of Law">USC Gould School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine_of_USC" title="Keck School of Medicine of USC">Keck School of Medicine of USC</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Thornton_School_of_Music" title="USC Thornton School of Music">USC Thornton School of Music</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=USC_School_of_Pharmacy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="USC School of Pharmacy (page does not exist)">USC School of Pharmacy</a>, USC <a href="/w/index.php?title=Price_School_of_Public_Policy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Price School of Public Policy (page does not exist)">Price School of Public Policy</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sowkweb.usc.edu/">USC School of Social Work</a>, and <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Theatre" title="USC School of Theatre" class="mw-redirect">USC School of Theatre</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USC_Student_Union.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/USC_Student_Union.jpg/220px-USC_Student_Union.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/USC_Student_Union.jpg/330px-USC_Student_Union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/USC_Student_Union.jpg/440px-USC_Student_Union.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USC_Student_Union.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> USC Gwynn Wilson Student Union
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Undergraduate Student Government (USG) makes decisions representing the undergraduate students of the university. It consists of an appointed executive leadership board, popularly elected legislative branch, and judicial oversight, along with a programming board (commonly referred to as &quot;Program Board&quot;). All USG activities are funded by the student activity fee, which the Treasurer has control over setting and that the Senate approves. In addition to USG, residents within university housing are represented and governed by the University Residential Student Community (URSC), which is divided by residence hall. The Graduate Student Government (GSG) consists of senators elected by the students of each school proportional to its enrollment and its activities are funded by a graduate and professional student activity fee.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_university_presidents">List of university presidents</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: List of university presidents">edit</a>]</span></h3>

      <li><a href="/wiki/John_R._Hubbard" title="John R. Hubbard">John R. Hubbard</a> (1970?1980)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/James_Zumberge" title="James Zumberge">James H. Zumberge</a> (1980?1991)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Steven_B._Sample" title="Steven B. Sample" class="mw-redirect">Steven B. Sample</a> (1991?2010)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/C._L._Max_Nikias" title="C. L. Max Nikias">C. L. Max Nikias</a> (2010?present)</li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California_academics" title="University of Southern California academics">University of Southern California academics</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USC_Law.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/USC_Law.jpg/220px-USC_Law.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/USC_Law.jpg/330px-USC_Law.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/USC_Law.jpg/440px-USC_Law.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USC_Law.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Law School building is one of the handful of examples of 
        <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist architecture</a> on the main campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>USC is a large, primarily residential research university.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of the student body was undergraduate until 2007, when graduate student enrollment began to exceed undergraduate.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The four-year, full-time undergraduate instructional program is classified as &quot;balanced arts &amp; sciences/professions&quot; with a high graduate coexistence. Admissions are characterized as &quot;most selective, lower transfer in&quot;; 95 undergraduate majors and 147 academic and professional minors are offered.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The graduate program is classified as &quot;comprehensive&quot; and offers 134 master's, doctoral, and professional degrees through 17 professional schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> USC is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> USC's academic departments fall either under the general <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">sciences</a> of the Dana and David Dornsife College of Letters, Arts, and Sciences for undergraduates, the Graduate School for graduates, or the university's 18 professional schools.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mudd_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Mudd_Hall.jpg/220px-Mudd_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Mudd_Hall.jpg/330px-Mudd_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Mudd_Hall.jpg/440px-Mudd_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mudd_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Mudd Hall of Philosophy
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The USC Dana and David Dornsife College of Letters, Arts, and Sciences, the oldest and largest of the USC schools, grants undergraduate degrees in more than 130 majors and minors across the humanities, social sciences, and natural/physical sciences, and offers doctoral and masters programs in more than 20 fields.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Dornsife College is responsible for the general education program for all USC undergraduates, and houses a full-time faculty of approximately 700, more than 6500 undergraduate majors (roughly half the total USC undergraduate population), and 1200 doctoral students. In addition to 30 academic departments, the College also houses dozens of research centers and institutes. In the 2008?2009 academic year, 4,400 undergraduate degrees and 5,500 advanced degrees were awarded. Formerly called &quot;USC College of Letters, Arts &amp; Sciences&quot;, the College received a $200 million gift from USC trustees Dana and David Dornsife on March 23, 2011, after which the College was renamed in their honor, following the naming pattern of other professional schools and departments at the University.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> All Ph.D. degrees awarded at USC and most masters degrees are under the jurisdiction of the Graduate School.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Professional degrees are awarded by each of the respective professional schools.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg/220px-USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg/330px-USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg/440px-USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> School of Cinematic Arts.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Cinematic_Arts" title="USC School of Cinematic Arts">The School of Cinematic Arts</a>, the oldest and largest film school in the country, confers degrees in six different programs.<sup id="cite_ref-LATcntv_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATcntv-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> As the university administration considered cinematic skills too valuable to be kept to film industry professionals, the school opened its classes to the university at large in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001, the film school added an <a href="/wiki/USC_Interactive_Media_Division" title="USC Interactive Media Division" class="mw-redirect">Interactive Media Division</a> studying stereoscopic cinema, panoramic cinema, immersive cinema, interactive cinema, video games, virtual reality, and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile</a> media. In September 2006, George Lucas donated $175 million to expand the film school, which at the time was the largest single donation to USC (and its fifth over $100 million). The donation will be used to build new structures and expand the faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The acceptance rate to the School of Cinematic Arts has consistently remained between 4-6% for the past several years.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/USC_School_of_Architecture" title="USC School of Architecture">USC School of Architecture</a> was established within the Roski School of Fine Arts in 1916, the first in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. This small department grew rapidly with the help of the Allied Architects of Los Angeles. A separate School of Architecture was organized in September 1925. The school has been home to teachers such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neutra" title="Richard Neutra">Richard Neutra</a>, Ralph Knowles, James Steele, <a href="/wiki/A._Quincy_Jones" title="A. Quincy Jones">A. Quincy Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Koenig" title="Pierre Koenig">Pierre Koenig</a>. The school of architecture also claims notable alumni <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Jerde" title="Jon Jerde">Jon Jerde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thom_Mayne" title="Thom Mayne">Thom Mayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Soriano" title="Raphael Soriano">Raphael Soriano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Ain" title="Gregory Ain">Gregory Ain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Koenig" title="Pierre Koenig">Pierre Koenig</a>. Two of the alumni have become <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_Prize" title="Pritzker Prize" class="mw-redirect">Pritzker Prize</a> winners. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Qingyun_Ma" title="Qingyun Ma">Qingyun Ma</a>, a distinguished Shanghai-based architect, was named dean of the school.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/USC_Thornton_School_of_Music" title="USC Thornton School of Music">USC Thornton School of Music</a> is one of the most highly regarded music schools in the United States. The training at the Thornton School frequently draws graduate students from such institutions including <a href="/wiki/Juilliard" title="Juilliard" class="mw-redirect">Juilliard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">Rice</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Eastman_School_of_Music" title="Eastman School of Music">Eastman School of Music</a>; and graduates of the Thornton School often go on to study at these and other institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Colburn_School" title="Colburn School">Colburn School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute_of_Music" title="Curtis Institute of Music">Curtis Institute of Music</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_School_of_Music" title="Manhattan School of Music">Manhattan School of Music</a>. The most active source of live music in all of Los Angeles, the Thornton School offers everything from medieval music to current music. In addition to the departments of classical music, there is a department for popular music and even a department of early music, making USC's music school one of the few in the United States that offers specialized degrees in pre-classical music.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Viterbi_School_of_Engineering" title="Viterbi School of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Andrew and Erna Viterbi School of Engineering</a> is headed by Dean <a href="/wiki/Yanis_C._Yortsos" title="Yanis C. Yortsos" class="mw-redirect">Yannis Yortsos</a>. Previously known as the USC School of Engineering, it was renamed on March 2, 2004, as the Andrew and Erna Viterbi School of Engineering in honor of <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Viterbi" title="Andrew Viterbi">Andrew Viterbi</a> and his wife Erna, who had donated $52 million to the school. Viterbi school of Engineering is ranked No.9 in the US as per the US News Rankings for engineering in 2013-14.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg/220px-052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg/330px-052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg/440px-052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:052707-020-USCAnnenberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Annenberg School for Communication &amp; Journalism
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California_Annenberg_School_for_Communication" title="University of Southern California Annenberg School for Communication" class="mw-redirect">Annenberg School for Communication &amp; Journalism</a>, founded in 1971 is one of the two communication programs in the country endowed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Annenberg" title="Walter Annenberg">Walter Annenberg</a> (the other is at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>). The School of Journalism, which became part of the School for Communication in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> features a core curriculum that requires students to devote themselves equally to print, broadcast and online media for the first year of study. The journalism school consistently ranks among the nation's top undergraduate journalism schools. <sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>USC's Annenberg School for Communication endowment rose from $7.5 million to $218 million between 1996 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Herman Ostrow School of Dentistry at the University of Southern California was established in 1897 as The College of Dentistry, and today awards undergraduate and graduate degrees. Headed by Dean Avishai Sadan, D.M.D., the school traditionally has maintained five Divisions: Academic Affairs &amp; Student Life, Clinical Affairs, Continuing Education, Research, and Community Health Programs and Hospital Affairs. In 2006, the USC Department of Physical Therapy and Biokinesiology, and the USC Department of Occupational Science and Occupational Therapy, which both had previously been organized as &quot;Independent Health Professions&quot; programs at USC's College of Letters, Arts, and Sciences, were administratively aligned under the School of Dentistry and renamed &quot;Divisions,&quot; bringing the total number of Divisions at the School of Dentistry to seven. In 2010, alumnus Herman Ostrow donated $35 million to name the school the Herman Ostrow School of Dentistry.</p> 
     <p>USC collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> to offer the USC (Executive) EMBA program in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>. USC also operates two international study centers in Paris and Madrid. The <a href="/wiki/Marshall_School_of_Business" title="Marshall School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Marshall School of Business</a> has satellite campuses in <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>.</p> 
     <p>In May 2006, USC's Board of Trustees and administration traveled to <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. to announce the establishment of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://china.usc.edu">USC U.S.-China Institute (USCI)</a>. USCI focuses on the multidimensional and evolving U.S?China relationship and trends in China. USCI has funded research into a variety of topics including the history of U.S.?China diplomatic exchanges, aging, property rights, environmental challenges, agricultural policy, new media, migration, and technology exchange. The Institute produced the highly regarded <i>Assignment:China<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></i> documentary series on American media coverage of China from the 1940s to today. It also publishes two magazines, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://uschina.usc.edu"><i>US-China Today</i></a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://asiapacificarts.usc.edu"><i>Asia Pacific Arts</i></a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_library_system">University library system</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: University library system">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California_libraries" title="University of Southern California libraries" class="mw-redirect">University of Southern California libraries</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Oldcollege1920.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Oldcollege1920.jpg/220px-Oldcollege1920.jpg" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Oldcollege1920.jpg/330px-Oldcollege1920.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Oldcollege1920.jpg/440px-Oldcollege1920.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Oldcollege1920.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The first true library was housed in the College of Liberal Arts Building (&quot;Old College&quot;), which was built in 1884, and designed to hold the entire USC student body?55 students. Two wings were added to the original building in 1905.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The USC Libraries are among the oldest private academic research libraries in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. For more than a century USC has been building collections in support of the university's teaching and research interests. Especially noteworthy collections include <a href="/wiki/American_literature" title="American literature">American literature</a>, Cinema-Television including the <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> studio archives, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerontology" title="Gerontology">gerontology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> exile literature, <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_studies" title="Korean studies">Korean studies</a>, studies of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_history" title="Natural history">natural history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> history, and the University Archives.</p> 
     <p>The USC Warner Bros. Archives is the largest single studio collection in the world. Donated in 1977 to the University of Southern California's School of Cinematic Arts, by Warner Communications, the WBA houses departmental records that detail Warner Bros. activities from the studio's first major feature, <i>My Four Years in Germany</i> (1918), to its sale to Seven Arts in 1968.</p> 
     <p>Announced in June 2006, the testimonies of 52,000 survivors, rescuers and others involved in the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> will now be housed in the USC College of Letters, Arts &amp; Sciences as a part of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/USC_Shoah_Foundation_Institute_for_Visual_History_and_Education" title="USC Shoah Foundation Institute for Visual History and Education">USC Shoah Foundation Institute for Visual History and Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition to the Shoah Foundation, the USC Libraries digital collection highlights include the California Historical Society, Korean American Archives and the Chinese Historical Society of Southern California. The digital archive holds 193,252 records and 223,487 content files of varying formats.</p> 
     <p>USC's 22 libraries and other archives currently hold nearly 4 million printed volumes, 6 million items in <a href="/wiki/Microform" title="Microform">microform</a>, and 3 million <a href="/wiki/Photographs" title="Photographs" class="mw-redirect">photographs</a> and subscribe to more than 30,000 current serial titles, nearly 44,000 feet (13,000&nbsp;m) of manuscripts and archives, and subscribe to over 120 electronic databases and more than 14,000 journals in print and electronic formats. Annually, reference transactions number close to 50,000 and approximately 1,100 instructional presentations are made to 16,000 participants.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Southern California Library system is among the top 35 largest university library systems in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p>In the U.S. News &amp; World Report's annual ranking of best &quot;National Universities,&quot; USC made the prestigious top 25 and was ranked 24th in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-USNWRRanking.pdf_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWRRanking.pdf-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usnews_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> USC is ranked 46th among world universities and 32nd among universities in the Americas by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>, 48th worldwide in 2011 by <i><a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and 13th (tied with seven other universities) among national universities by The Center for Measuring University Performance.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>USNWR</i> ranks USC's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California_Law_School" title="University of Southern California Law School" class="mw-redirect">School of Law</a> 18th,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_School_of_Business" title="Marshall School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Marshall School of Business</a> is ranked 9th in undergraduate education with the <a href="/wiki/USC_Leventhal_School_of_Accounting" title="USC Leventhal School of Accounting" class="mw-redirect">USC Leventhal School of Accounting</a> 4th, the Lloyd Greif Center for Entrepreneurial Studies 3rd and 20th for its MBA program,<sup id="cite_ref-Top_Business_Schools_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Business_Schools-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Keck_School_of_Medicine_of_USC" title="Keck School of Medicine of USC">Keck School of Medicine of USC</a> 34th in research and unranked in primary care,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Viterbi_School_of_Engineering" title="Viterbi School of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Viterbi School of Engineering</a> 11th,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Rossier_School_of_Education" title="Rossier School of Education" class="mw-redirect">Rossier School of Education</a> 14th,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Roski School of Fine arts Graduate program 37th,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/USC_Sol_Price_School_of_Public_Policy" title="USC Sol Price School of Public Policy">Sol Price School of Public Policy</a> 7th,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> the USC School of Social Work 8th. The <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Gourmet_Report" title="Philosophical Gourmet Report">Philosophical Gourmet Report</a> ranks USC's graduate philosophy program as 11th nationally,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>USC was named &quot;College of the Year 2000&quot; by the editors of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> for the university's extensive community-service programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Time.2FPrinceton_Review_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time.2FPrinceton_Review-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>&quot;The Hollywood Reporter&quot; ranked USC School of Cinematic Arts the #1 film school in the world, beating out the &quot;American Film Institute&quot; and &quot;UCLA&quot;-- two schools who have been previous top contenders. <span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/hollywood-reporter-top-25-film-schools-usc-ucla-afi-353726">&quot;Top Film Schools&quot;</a>. The Hollywood Reporter. 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2012-07-25</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Southern+California&amp;rft.btitle=Top+Film+Schools&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.hollywoodreporter.com%2Fnews%2Fhollywood-reporter-top-25-film-schools-usc-ucla-afi-353726&amp;rft.pub=The+Hollywood+Reporter&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></p> 
     <p><i>The Princeton Review</i> ranked USC video game design program as 1st out of 150 schools in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's video game design programs are interdisciplinary, involving the Interactive Media Division of the USC School of Cinematic Arts and the GamePipe program in the Department of Computer Science at the USC Viterbi School of Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Institute of Higher Education at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> ranked USC's combined departments of engineering and computer sciences as 11th in the world, physical sciences 52nd, social sciences 35th, life sciences 51st, clinical medicine and pharmacy 47th.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai-med_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-med-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> USC is also among top 10 dream colleges in the United States. Princeton Review's &quot;College Hopes &amp; Worries&quot; 2010 survey reports USC as the 9th dream college for both students and parents separately.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p>USC has a total enrollment of 36,896 students, of which 17,380 are at the undergraduate and 19,516 at the graduate and professional levels.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The male-female ratio at USC is nearly 1:1. 31.2% of incoming students are drawn from the greater Los Angeles metropolitan area, 20.9% from other areas in California, 39.5% from the rest of the United States, and 8.4% from abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> USC's student body encompasses 7,115 international students, more than any other university in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> and the university maintains offices in several countries.<sup class="reference" id="ref_Bnone"><a href="#endnote_Bnone">[b]</a></sup> There are approximately 200,000 living <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Southern_California_people" title="List of University of Southern California people">Trojan Alumni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USC-all-students_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USC-all-students-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3>
