     <p>37,210 students applied for admission to the undergraduate class of 2015, with 8,566 being admitted (23%) and 2,931 enrolling (34% yield). Among admitted students, the <a href="/wiki/Interquartile_range" title="Interquartile range">interquartile range</a> for <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> composite scores was 2020-2240<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> and the average unweighted GPA was 3.80, while among enrolled freshmen, the SAT range was 1970-2180 and the average GPA was 3.72.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> 20 percent of admitted and attending students are SCions, or students with familial ties to USC, while 14 percent are the first generation in their family to attend any form of college. There were also 247 <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholarship_Program" title="National Merit Scholarship Program">National Merit Scholar</a> winners and 7 National Achievement Scholars in the admitted class. USC ranks among the top five schools in the nation in terms of its enrollment of National Merit Scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> USC's admission rate has dropped to 20% for the class of 2016, following its adoption of the Common Application.</p> 
     <p>2012-2013 Undergraduate Estimate of Costs at USC Tuition $43,722 Mandatory fees $741 Room and board* 12,440 Books and supplies $1,500 Personal and miscellaneous $900 Transportation $580.00 Total $59,883 + $150 USC Orientation fee for the 1st semester</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_research">Faculty and research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Faculty and research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg/220px-052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg/330px-052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg/440px-052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:052707-022-NorrisCinema-USC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Eileen L. Norris Cinema Theatre, where the 
        <a href="/wiki/THX" title="THX">THX</a> sound system was first developed and installed by Tomlinson Holman.
        <sup id="cite_ref-USCselftour_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCselftour-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>USC employs approximately 3,249 full-time faculty, 1,486 part-time faculty, and about 10,744 staff members.<sup id="cite_ref-0910FacSta_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-0910FacSta-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> 350 postdoctoral fellows are supported along with over 800 medical residents.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the USC faculty, 12 have been elected to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Science" title="National Academy of Science" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Science</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NatAcadMembers_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatAcadMembers-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> 35 to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NatAcadMembers_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatAcadMembers-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> 13 to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NatAcadMembers_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatAcadMembers-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> 21 to the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MiscAcadMembers_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiscAcadMembers-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> 75 to the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MiscAcadMembers_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiscAcadMembers-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> 6 to the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MiscAcadMembers_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiscAcadMembers-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and 9 to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Public_Administration_(United_States)" title="National Academy of Public Administration (United States)">National Academy of Public Administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MiscAcadMembers_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiscAcadMembers-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> 29 USC faculty are listed as among the &quot;Highly Cited&quot; in the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Scientific_Information" title="Institute for Scientific Information">Institute for Scientific Information</a> database.<sup id="cite_ref-HighlyCitedUSC_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HighlyCitedUSC-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Olah" title="George Olah" class="mw-redirect">George Olah</a> won the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> and directs the <a href="/wiki/Loker_Hydrocarbon_Research_Institute" title="Loker Hydrocarbon Research Institute">Loker Hydrocarbon Research Institute</a>. <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Adleman" title="Leonard Adleman">Leonard Adleman</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In fiscal year 2007 USC expended $415.2 million on research, and major funding came from federal agencies: the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="Department of Health and Human Services" class="mw-redirect">Department of Health and Human Services</a> granted $182.4 million, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a> $45.7 million, and <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> $41.8 million.<sup id="cite_ref-DCG_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCG-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Total foundation and association sponsorship totaled $43.1 million, corporate research $30.6 million, and local government funding totaled $28.1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-DCG_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCG-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also supports the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Council_on_International_Policy" title="Pacific Council on International Policy">Pacific Council on International Policy</a> through joint programming, leadership collaboration, and facilitated connections among students, faculty, and Pacific Council members.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has two <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>?funded Engineering Research Centers: the <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Media_Systems_Center" title="Integrated Media Systems Center">Integrated Media Systems Center</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biomimetic_Microelectronic_Systems" title="Center for Biomimetic Microelectronic Systems">Center for Biomimetic Microelectronic Systems</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> selected USC as its first Homeland Security Center of Excellence. Since 1991, USC has been the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">NSF</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">USGS</a> funded <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Earthquake_Center" title="Southern California Earthquake Center">Southern California Earthquake Center</a> (SCEC). The University of Southern California is a founding and charter member of <a href="/wiki/CENIC" title="CENIC" class="mw-redirect">CENIC</a>, the Corporation for Education Network Initiatives in California, the nonprofit organization, which provides extremely high-performance Internet-based networking to California's K-20 research and education community. USC researcher <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Postel" title="Jonathan Postel" class="mw-redirect">Jonathan Postel</a> was an editor of communications-protocol for the fledgling internet, also known as <a href="/wiki/ARPANET" title="ARPANET">ARPANET</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable USC faculty include or have included the following: <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Adleman" title="Leonard Adleman">Leonard Adleman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bellman" title="Richard Bellman" class="mw-redirect">Richard Bellman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aimee_Bender" title="Aimee Bender">Aimee Bender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Boehm" title="Barry Boehm">Barry Boehm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Bennis" title="Warren Bennis">Warren Bennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Boyd" title="Todd Boyd">Todd Boyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/T.C._Boyle" title="T.C. Boyle" class="mw-redirect">T.C. Boyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Buscaglia" title="Leo Buscaglia">Leo Buscaglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drew_Casper" title="Drew Casper">Drew Casper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Castells" title="Manuel Castells">Manuel Castells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Chemerinsky" title="Erwin Chemerinsky">Erwin Chemerinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Crow" title="Thomas E. Crow">Thomas Crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Dam%C3%A1sio" title="Ant&oacute;nio Dam&aacute;sio" class="mw-redirect">Ant&oacute;nio Dam&aacute;sio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_De_Erdely" title="Francis De Erdely" class="mw-redirect">Francis De Erdely</a>, <a href="/wiki/Percival_Everett" title="Percival Everett">Percival Everett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gell-Mann" title="Murray Gell-Mann">Murray Gell-Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Ginsburg" title="Seymour Ginsburg">Seymour Ginsburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/G._Thomas_Goodnight" title="G. Thomas Goodnight">G. Thomas Goodnight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Goodall" title="Jane Goodall">Jane Goodall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Golomb" title="Solomon Golomb" class="mw-redirect">Solomon Golomb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Estrich" title="Susan Estrich">Susan Estrich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janet_Fitch" title="Janet Fitch">Janet Fitch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomlinson_Holman" title="Tomlinson Holman">Tomlinson Holman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Jenkins" title="Henry Jenkins">Henry Jenkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_H._Jordan" title="Thomas H. Jordan">Thomas H. Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Koenig" title="Pierre Koenig">Pierre Koenig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Leach" title="Neil Leach">Neil Leach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Maltin" title="Leonard Maltin">Leonard Maltin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_L._McFadden" title="Daniel L. McFadden" class="mw-redirect">Daniel L. McFadden</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Olah" title="George Olah" class="mw-redirect">George Olah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Orfalea" title="Paul Orfalea">Paul Orfalea</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_V._Chilingar" title="George V. Chilingar">George V. Chilingar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Ramo" title="Simon Ramo">Simon Ramo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irving_S._Reed" title="Irving S. Reed">Irving Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Waterman" title="Michael Waterman">Michael Waterman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arieh_Warshel" title="Arieh Warshel">Arieh Warshel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_R._Welch" title="Lloyd R. Welch">Lloyd Welch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Taplin" title="Jonathan Taplin">Jonathan Taplin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diane_Winston_(professor)" title="Diane Winston (professor)">Diane Winston</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Southern_California_people" title="List of University of Southern California people">List of University of Southern California people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>There are currently 200,000 living <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Southern_California_people" title="List of University of Southern California people">Trojan alumni</a>, with nearly 75% of all alumni living in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usc.edu_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usc.edu-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Southern_California_people" title="List of University of Southern California people">notable alumni of the University of Southern California</a> have become prominent scientists, musicians, businessmen, engineers, architects, athletes, actors, politicians, and those that have gained both national and international fame. To keep alumni connected, the Trojan network consists of over 100 alumni groups on five continents. A common saying among those associated with the school is that one is a &quot;Trojan for Life&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Among notable alumni are <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">Neil Armstrong</a>, the first human to step on the moon, <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>, creator of the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a> trilogy, and Dr. <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Morsi" title="Mohamed Morsi">Mohamed Morsi</a>, the first ever <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratically elected</a> president in the history of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-victory_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-victory-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans" title="USC Trojans">USC Trojans</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg/220px-11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg/330px-11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg/440px-11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:11-11-06-GalenCenter-inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Galen Center, home of USC basketball and volleyball
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The USC Trojans participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I (FBS)</a> <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a> and has won 115 total team national championships (non-NCAA and NCAA): 92 for men and 23 for women. Of this total, 80 and 14 are <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> National Championships for men and women, respectively. The NCAA does not include <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> championships in its calculation. Though there are multiple organizations that name national championships, USC claims 11 football championships. The men's 361 Individual Championships are the second-best in the nation and 53 ahead of third place <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas" title="University of Texas" class="mw-redirect">Texas</a>. USC's cross-town rival is <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>, with whom there is fierce athletic and scholastic competition. USC's rivalry with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a>?though generally limited to football?predates the <a href="/wiki/UCLA-USC_rivalry" title="UCLA-USC rivalry" class="mw-redirect">UCLA rivalry</a> by three years. The Notre Dame rivalry stems mainly from the annual <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> game played between these two universities and is considered one of the greatest rivalries in college athletics.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>USC has won 96 NCAA team championships, 3rd behind cross-town rival UCLA (108) and Stanford (103). The Trojans have also won at least one national team title in 26 consecutive years (1959?60 to 1984?85). USC won the National College All-Sports Championship, an annual ranking by <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a> of the country's top athletic programs, 6 times since its inception in 1971. Four Trojans have won the <a href="/wiki/James_E._Sullivan_Award" title="James E. Sullivan Award">James E. Sullivan Award</a> as the top amateur athlete in America: diver <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Lee_(diver)" title="Sammy Lee (diver)">Sammy Lee</a> (1953), shot putter <a href="/wiki/Parry_O%27Brien" title="Parry O'Brien">Parry O'Brien</a> (1959), swimmer <a href="/wiki/John_Naber" title="John Naber">John Naber</a> (1977) and swimmer <a href="/wiki/Janet_Evans" title="Janet Evans">Janet Evans</a> (1989).</p> 
     <p>From the 1904 <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" title="Summer Olympics" class="mw-redirect">Summer Olympics</a> through the 2008 games, 393 Trojan athletes have competed in the Games, taking home 122 <a href="/wiki/Gold_medals" title="Gold medals" class="mw-redirect">gold medals</a>, 76 <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> and 60 <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> If it were an independent country, USC would be ranked <a href="/wiki/All-time_Olympic_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Olympic Games medal table">12th in the world</a> in terms of medals.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1912, USC is the only university in the world to have a gold medal-winning athlete in every summer Olympiad.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalogue_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalogue-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_sports">Men's sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Men's sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg/220px-11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg/330px-11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg/440px-11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:11-11-06-LA-Coliseum-USC-UO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum during a USC football game
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In men's sports, USC has won 93 team national championships (80 NCAA titles) - more than any other school - and male athletes have won a record 303 individual NCAA titles. The Trojans have won 26 championships in <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, 19 in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Tennis_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Tennis Championship">tennis</a>, 12 in <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">baseball</a>, 9 in <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, 7 in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Water_Polo_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Water Polo Championship">water polo</a>, 6 in <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, 2 in indoor track and field, and 1 in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Gymnastics_championship" title="NCAA Men's Gymnastics championship" class="mw-redirect">gymnastics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="ref_Cnone"><a href="#endnote_Cnone">[c]</a></sup> USC's men's basketball has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA tournament</a> 15 times, and made 2 NCAA <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> appearances.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_football" title="USC Trojans football">USC football program</a> has consistently ranked among the best in the <a href="/wiki/Division_I_FBS" title="Division I FBS" class="mw-redirect">Division I FBS</a> in recent years. During the term of <a href="/wiki/Pete_Carroll" title="Pete Carroll">Pete Carroll</a> as head coach, the Trojans improved their rankings and competed in a variety of <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowls</a> and championships. The Trojans football team has won 11 national championships.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Seven players have won the <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a>, although the school claims six, after alleged violations involving Reggie Bush. As of 2011, 472 Trojans have been taken in the <a href="/wiki/NFL_Draft" title="NFL Draft" class="mw-redirect">NFL Draft</a>, more than any other university.<sup id="cite_ref-USCdraftrecord_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCdraftrecord-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_sports">Women's sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Women's sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Women's teams have earned 23 national championships. The Women of Troy have brought home 64 individual NCAA crowns. Two Women of Troy athletes have won the <a href="/wiki/Honda-Broderick_Cup" title="Honda-Broderick Cup">Honda-Broderick Cup</a> as the top collegiate woman athlete of the year: <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Miller" title="Cheryl Miller">Cheryl Miller</a> (1983?84) and <a href="/wiki/Angela_Williams" title="Angela Williams">Angela Williams</a> (2001?02). And Trojan women have won 8 <a href="/wiki/Honda_Sports_Award" title="Honda Sports Award">Honda Awards</a>, as the top female athlete in their sport.</p> 
     <p>The Women of Troy have won 7 championships in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Tennis_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Tennis Championship">tennis</a>, 6 in <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, 3 in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Water_Polo_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Water Polo Championship">water polo</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Championship">basketball</a>, 1 in <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, 1 in <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, and 1 in <a href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer" class="mw-redirect">soccer</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions_and_student_activities">Traditions and student activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Traditions and student activities">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Usctravelerandband.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Usctravelerandband.jpg/220px-Usctravelerandband.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Usctravelerandband.jpg/330px-Usctravelerandband.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Usctravelerandband.jpg/440px-Usctravelerandband.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Usctravelerandband.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> USC mascot Traveler with Trojan Warrior and The Spirit of Troy
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As one of the oldest universities in California, the University of Southern California has a long and storied history resulting in a number of modern traditions, some of which are outlined here:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>USC's official <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is &quot;<a href="/wiki/Fight_On" title="Fight On">Fight On</a>&quot;, which was composed in 1922 by USC dental student Milo Sweet (with lyrics by Sweet and Glen Grant).</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg/170px-120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg/255px-120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg/340px-120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:120107-LA-USC-UCLA02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> During the week prior to the traditional USC-UCLA rivalry football game, the 
        <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Trojan" title="Tommy Trojan">Tommy Trojan</a> statue is covered to prevent UCLA vandalism.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_%E2%80%93_USC_rivalry" title="Notre Dame ? USC rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Notre Dame ? USC rivalry</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/UCLA%E2%80%93USC_rivalry" title="UCLA?USC rivalry">UCLA?USC rivalry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>USC has rivalries with multiple schools. Though generally limited to football, USC has a major rivalry with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a>. The annual game is played for the <a href="/wiki/Jeweled_Shillelagh" title="Jeweled Shillelagh">Jeweled Shillelagh</a>. The rivalry has featured more national championship teams, Heisman trophy winners, All-Americans, and future NFL hall-of-famers than any other collegiate match-up. The two schools have kept the annual game on their schedules since 1926 (except 1942?44 because of World War II travel restrictions) and the game is often referred to as the greatest intersectional rivalry in college football.<sup id="cite_ref-SI101305_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SI101305-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ESPN112406_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN112406-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SI101205_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SI101205-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT102007_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT102007-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PAC112006_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAC112006-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>USC's cross-town rival is UCLA, with whom there is fierce athletic and scholastic competition. Both are within L.A. city limits, approximately 10 miles (16&nbsp;km) apart. Until 1982 the two schools also shared the same football stadium, the Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum. The victor of the annual football game takes home the <a href="/wiki/Victory_Bell_(USC-UCLA)" title="Victory Bell (USC-UCLA)" class="mw-redirect">Victory Bell</a>. The Trojans and Bruins also compete in a year-long all-sports competition for the <a href="/wiki/Lexus_Gauntlet_Trophy" title="Lexus Gauntlet Trophy" class="mw-redirect">Lexus Gauntlet Trophy</a>. Pranks between <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and USC were commonplace several decades ago. Both universities have cracked down on pranks since a 1989 incident when USC students released hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Cricket_(insect)" title="Cricket (insect)">crickets</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Powell_Library" title="Powell Library">main UCLA library</a> during finals week.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Days before a clash between rivals <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and USC in 2009, the Bruins mascot was vandalized. It was splashed in cardinal and gold paint, USC's official colors sparking memories of pranks played in the years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The week preceding the annual football matchup with UCLA is known as &quot;Troy Week&quot; and features a number of traditions including CONQUEST! &quot;The Ultimate Trojan Experience&quot;, Save Tommy Night, the CONQUEST! Bonfire, and all-night vigils by the <a href="/wiki/Trojan_Knights" title="Trojan Knights">Trojan Knights</a> to protect the campus from <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">UCLA Bruins</a>.</p> 
     <p>In addition, USC has rivalries with other Pac-12 schools, particularly <a href="/wiki/Stanford" title="Stanford" class="mw-redirect">Stanford</a> as they are the only two private universities in the conference and are situated at opposing regions of California, as well as being the two oldest private research universities in California, 1880 and 1891 respectively. Recently, a rivalry has begun to exist between USC and the University of Oregon because of the two universities' dominant football programs, with each school often serving as the toughest match-up on the opponent's schedule.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots">Mascots</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mascots">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Traveler, a white <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_horse" title="Andalusian horse">Andalusian horse</a>, is currently the university's official mascot. It first appeared at a football game in 1961, and was known at Traveler I. The current horse is known as Traveler VII.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Trojan" title="Tommy Trojan">Tommy Trojan</a>, officially known as the Trojan Shrine, is a bronze statue in the model of a <a href="/wiki/Troy" title="Troy">Trojan</a> warrior at the center of campus. It is commonly mistaken as the school's official mascot. The statue was modeled after Trojan football players, and the statue is engraved with the ideal characteristics of a Trojan. It is a popular meeting point for students and a landmark for visitors.</p> 
     <p>In the 1940s, <a href="/wiki/George_Tirebiter" title="George Tirebiter">George Tirebiter</a>, a car-chasing dog, was the most popular unofficial mascot. After it bit the mascot of the UCLA Bruins, it gained fame among students. The dog was known to chase down cars on Trousdale Parkway, which runs through campus. After the original dog died, a few others succeeded it. A statue was built in 2006 to honor the unofficial mascot.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marching_band">Marching band</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Marching band">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg/220px-2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg/330px-2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg/440px-2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2008-0830-USC-UVA-TMB-drummajor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The drum major of the Spirit of Troy wears a more elaborate uniform and conducts the band with a sword.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>USC's <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Spirit_of_Troy" title="Spirit of Troy">The Spirit of Troy</a>, has been featured in at least 10 major <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">movies</a>, and has performed in both the <a href="/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics" title="1932 Summer Olympics">1932</a> and <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 Summer Olympics</a> in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> They have also performed on television shows and with other musicians.</p> 
     <p>The band performed on the title track of the <a href="/wiki/1979_in_music" title="1979 in music">1979</a> <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood_Mac" title="Fleetwood Mac">Fleetwood Mac</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Tusk_(album)" title="Tusk (album)">Tusk</a></i>, which went on to be a <a href="/wiki/Platinum_record" title="Platinum record" class="mw-redirect">multi-platinum record</a>. In 1990, the band performed live on <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Funniest_Home_Videos" title="America's Funniest Home Videos">America's Funniest Home Videos</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the band later played on another multi-platinum Fleetwood Mac album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dance_(Fleetwood_Mac_album)" title="The Dance (Fleetwood Mac album)">The Dance</a></i> (1997).<sup id="cite_ref-FleetwoodPlat_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FleetwoodPlat-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The Spirit of Troy is the only collegiate band to have two platinum records.<sup id="cite_ref-DT081804_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT081804-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMBnotes_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMBnotes-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent years, the band has appeared at the <a href="/wiki/51st_Grammy_Award" title="51st Grammy Award" class="mw-redirect">2009 Grammy Awards</a>, accompanying <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>; on the <a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">2009 Academy Awards</a> with <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles" title="Beyonc&eacute; Knowles">Beyonc&eacute; Knowles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Jackman" title="Hugh Jackman">Hugh Jackman</a>; and during the finale of <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a> 2008, backing <a href="/wiki/Renaldo_Lapuz" title="Renaldo Lapuz">Renaldo Lapuz</a> in instrumentation of his original song &quot;We're Brothers Forever.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-LAT020709_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT020709-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT022609_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT022609-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT052108_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT052108-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the band played on the show <a href="/wiki/Dancing_With_the_Stars" title="Dancing With the Stars" class="mw-redirect">Dancing With the Stars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC092909_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC092909-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The USC band was only one of two American groups invited to march in the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> parade in 2003 and 2004. The Trojan Marching Band performed at the 2005 World Expo in <a href="/wiki/Nagoya,_Aichi" title="Nagoya, Aichi" class="mw-redirect">Nagoya, Japan</a>. In May 2006, the Trojan Marching Band traveled to <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, performing once in Florence, and twice in Rome (including in front of the Coliseum). The band has also, for many years, performed the <a href="/wiki/1812_Overture" title="1812 Overture">1812 Overture</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Los Angeles Philharmonic Orchestra" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles Philharmonic Orchestra</a> (or occasionally with other orchestras) each year at the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a> &quot;Tchaikovsky Spectacular&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT082707_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT082707-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spirit_groups">Spirit groups</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spirit groups">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg/220px-091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg/330px-091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg/440px-091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:091507-USCNeb-SongGirls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Song Girls celebrating a USC Trojans football victory
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Founded in 1967, the USC Song Girls appear at all football, basketball, and volleyball games as well as rallies, university and alumni functions.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike other college cheer teams, Song Girls are primarily a dance squad and do not perform gymnastics, stunts or lead cheers.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1919, the USC Yell Leaders worked closely with The Spirit of Troy (USC Band) and the Song Girls to lead cheers and perform stunts to rally Trojan fans at football, basketball, and volleyball games. The sweater-clad team consisted of all men for most of its existence, though the squad later opened itself up to applicants from both sexes and did feature one female Yell Leader in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> They were disbanded by the University after the 2005?06 season and replaced by the co-ed Spirit Leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Trojan" title="Daily Trojan">Daily Trojan</a></i> has been the student <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a> of USC since 1912 and is a primary source of news and information for the campus. It secured the first interview of President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> after his resignation. The publication does not receive financial aid from the university and instead runs entirely on advertisement revenue. Published from Monday to Friday during the fall and spring semesters, the newspaper turns into the Summer Trojan during the summer term and publishes once a week. It is the paper of record on campus.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Trojan_Vision" title="Trojan Vision">Trojan Vision</a></i> (often abbreviated as <i>TV8</i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Student_television_station" title="Student television station">Student television station</a> at USC. TV8 was established in 1997 by the <a href="/wiki/USC_Annenberg_School_for_Communication_and_Journalism" title="USC Annenberg School for Communication and Journalism">Annenberg School for Communication</a>, but is now a part of the School of Cinematic Arts. Trojan Vision broadcasts 24/7 from the Robert Zemeckis Center for Digital Arts to the University Park Campus on Channel 8.1 and online through their website. Programming is also made available to the greater Los Angeles community on local channel LA36. In addition to a selection of regularly airing shows of many genres, Trojan Vision also broadcasts the shows <i>Platforum</i>, a round-table debate show; <i><a href="/wiki/Annenberg_TV_News" title="Annenberg TV News">Annenberg TV News</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/News_program" title="News program">news program</a>; and <i>CU@USC</i>, an interview program, live every weeknight from 5:30 pm to 7:00 pm.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>El Rodeo</i> is USC's student-run <a href="/wiki/Yearbook" title="Yearbook">yearbook</a>. One of the oldest student traditions at the university, the first edition was released in 1889 and was originally called <i>The Sybil</i>. The name was changed to <i>El Rodeo</i> in 1899 to reflect the cowboy-themed events students threw to advertise the yearbook as a &quot;roundup&quot; of the year's events. It was long packaged with the Student Activity Card, which gave students access to all home sports games. Since the card was dissolved in 2007, the yearbook has been sold as a stand-alone item.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Neon_Tommy" title="Neon Tommy">Neon Tommy</a></i> is a <a href="/wiki/News_website" title="News website" class="mw-redirect">news website</a> and <a href="/wiki/Content_aggregator" title="Content aggregator" class="mw-redirect">content aggregator</a> in the <a href="/wiki/USC_Annenberg_School_for_Communication_and_Journalism" title="USC Annenberg School for Communication and Journalism">USC Annenberg School for Communication and Journalism</a>. It is a web-only publication that was created in 2009. It does not cover campus news.</p> 
     <p><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sackoftroy.com">The Sack of Troy</a></i> is an online <a href="/wiki/News_satire" title="News satire">news satire</a> publication. It was started by USC students and is indepentently run.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">Greek Community</a>, making up approximately a fifth of the student body, has had a long and influential history on the campus. Centered on a portion of West 28th Street known as &quot;The Row&quot;, located between <a href="/wiki/Figueroa_Street" title="Figueroa Street">Figueroa Street</a> and Hoover Street just north of campus, USC's Greek system began soon after the school's founding when <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a> founded a chapter in 1887.</p> 
     <p>With 23 fraternities and 11 sororities in the <a href="/wiki/Interfraternity_Conference" title="Interfraternity Conference" class="mw-redirect">Interfraternity Conference</a> (IFC) and <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">Panhellenic Conference</a> (PHC), respectively, the USC Greek community has over 2,650 members and is one of the largest on the West Coast. It regularly participates in Homecoming and Songfest, and the community's philanthropic efforts and success in philanthropic leadership annually raise over $150,000.</p> 
     <p>Outside of the Panhellenic and Interfraternity conferences, the Greek community at USC is very diverse, boasting the Multicultural, Asian, Inter-Fraternity (composed of professional fraternities), and the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic</a> (historically black) Councils. Organizations governed by these councils include chapters of some of the oldest Latino and Black Greek organizations in the country and the oldest Asian fraternity in Southern California; while also including established professional business, engineering, and pre-law fraternities and other multiculturally based groups.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_media">Popular media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Popular media">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uscvkcnight2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Uscvkcnight2007.jpg/220px-Uscvkcnight2007.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Uscvkcnight2007.jpg/330px-Uscvkcnight2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Uscvkcnight2007.jpg/440px-Uscvkcnight2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uscvkcnight2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Fountain outside of Doheny Library with the Von KleinSmid Center; both buildings were used in the film 
        <i>The Graduate</i> as stand-ins for 
        <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Because of USC's proximity to <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_California" title="Hollywood, California" class="mw-redirect">Hollywood</a>, close ties between the School of Cinematic Arts and entertainment industry, and the architecture on campus, the university has been used in numerous movies, television series, commercials, and music videos. USC is frequently used by filmmakers, standing in for numerous other universities.</p> 
     <p>Movies filmed at USC include <i><a href="/wiki/Forrest_Gump" title="Forrest Gump">Forrest Gump</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde">Legally Blonde</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Road_Trip_(film)" title="Road Trip (film)">Road Trip</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Girl_Next_Door_(2004_film)" title="The Girl Next Door (2004 film)">The Girl Next Door</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harold_%26_Kumar_Go_to_White_Castle" title="Harold &amp; Kumar Go to White Castle">Harold &amp; Kumar Go to White Castle</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Love_%26_Basketball" title="Love &amp; Basketball">Love &amp; Basketball</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Chips" title="Blue Chips">Blue Chips</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ghostbusters" title="Ghostbusters">Ghostbusters</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Free_or_Die_Hard" title="Live Free or Die Hard">Live Free or Die Hard</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/House_Party_2" title="House Party 2">House Party 2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Number_23" title="The Number 23">The Number 23</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Graduate" title="The Graduate">The Graduate</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Television series that have used the USC campus include <i><a href="/wiki/Cold_Case_(TV_series)" title="Cold Case (TV series)" class="mw-redirect">Cold Case</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Entourage_(TV_series)" title="Entourage (TV series)">Entourage</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/24_(TV_series)" title="24 (TV series)">24</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_O.C." title="The O.C.">The O.C.</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_90210" title="Beverly Hills, 90210">Beverly Hills, 90210</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Moesha" title="Moesha">Moesha</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Saved_by_the_Bell:_The_College_Years" title="Saved by the Bell: The College Years">Saved by the Bell: The College Years</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fresh_Prince_of_Bel-Air" title="The Fresh Prince of Bel-Air">The Fresh Prince of Bel-Air</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/House_(TV_series)" title="House (TV series)">House M.D.</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_NY" title="CSI: NY">CSI: NY</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Undeclared" title="Undeclared">Undeclared</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alias_(TV_series)" title="Alias (TV series)">Alias</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Office_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Office (U.S. TV series)">The Office</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Monk_(TV_series)" title="Monk (TV series)">Monk</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_United_States_of_Tara" title="The United States of Tara" class="mw-redirect">The United States of Tara</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gilmore_Girls" title="Gilmore Girls">Gilmore Girls</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Scrubs_(TV_Series)" title="Scrubs (TV Series)" class="mw-redirect">Scrubs</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Roommate" title="The Roommate">The Roommate</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The USC campus also appears on the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Club:_Los_Angeles" title="Midnight Club: Los Angeles">Midnight Club: Los Angeles</a></i> on its &quot;South Central Map Expansion&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Midnight_Club:_Los_Angeles_South_Central_USC_campus_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Midnight_Club:_Los_Angeles_South_Central_USC_campus-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The campus has also served as a backdrop for television game shows <i><a href="/wiki/Jeopardy!" title="Jeopardy!">Jeopardy!</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wheel_of_Fortune_(US_game_show)" title="Wheel of Fortune (US game show)" class="mw-redirect">Wheel of Fortune</a></i>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other television series that have been filmed on campus include a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries,_2004" title="Democratic Party presidential primaries, 2004">2004 Democratic Party presidential candidates' debate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hardball_with_Chris_Matthews" title="Hardball with Chris Matthews">Hardball with Chris Matthews</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scholar" title="The Scholar">The Scholar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Best_Damn_Sports_Show_Period" title="The Best Damn Sports Show Period">The Best Damn Sports Show Period</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/College_GameDay_(football)" title="College GameDay (football)">College GameDay</a></i>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources.      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="refbegin references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 80em; -webkit-column-width: 80em; column-width: 80em;"> 
      <p><b>b.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Anone"><a href="#ref_Anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> These other names include <b>SC</b>, <b>Southern California</b>, and <b>Southern Cal</b>. Despite its prevalent use in sports-related articles, the official position of USC discourages use of &quot;Southern Cal&quot; (to reinforce the nonexistence of a foundational association in any context to <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Cal</a>), as clearly stated in all <a href="/wiki/Media_guide" title="Media guide">media guides</a>: &quot;Note to the media: In editorial references to athletic teams of the University of Southern California, the following are preferred: USC, Southern California, So. California, Troy and Trojans for men's or women's teams, and Women of Troy for women's teams. PLEASE do not use Southern Cal (it's like calling San Francisco 'Frisco' or North Carolina 'North Car.'). The usage of 'Southern Cal' on licensed apparel and merchandise is limited in scope and necessary to protect federal <a href="/wiki/Trademark" title="Trademark">trademark</a> rights.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-notsoutherncal_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notsoutherncal-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
      <p><b>c.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Bnone"><a href="#ref_Bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Specifically <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, China; <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.usc.edu/dept/International_Offices/">USC International Offices</a></p> 
      <p><b>d.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Cnone"><a href="#ref_Cnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The NCAA does not conduct a championship for Football Bowl Subdivision football. Instead, teams are awarded championships by various private organizations, currently the recognized championships are awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a> and titles by the <a href="/wiki/AP_Poll" title="AP Poll">Associated Press</a>.</p> 
      <p><b>e.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Dnone"><a href="#ref_Dnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The precise colors can be found on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.usc.edu/identity/print/colors_and_typefaces/">USC Graphic Identity Program website</a>: the correct <a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> color for USC Cardinal is PMS 201C and USC Gold is PMS 123C.</p> 
     </div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_and_notes">References and notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Southern_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: References and notes">edit</a>]</span></h2>
